A Word Gained 162

— Qiu Shui

▲ Money is the most important thing in the world. The happiness of individuals, or the morality of countries, is based on money.

▲ Time is of great importance to women. A woman of twenty years old can conquer a man with just a flash in his eyes. However, after another ten years, some kind of technique must be used to internally move any man.

▲ You cannot determine a man's love by the heat with which he kisses his wife. However, when he refuses to kiss other women within the realm of possibility, the extent of his love can be seen.

▲ A woman of twenty has the beauty of innocence. If a woman of forty does not have a natural heterogeneity, her beauty is completely artificial.

▲ If a man can choose his girlfriend very carefully, like choosing a cigar, then the lawyers who specialize in divorce cases in the society can all starve to death.

▲ If the top bookstores in the country can be pragmatic and drastically reduce prices for three years, then the knowledge of the general public can be greatly improved.

▲ A rich man without a certain belief or without a certain profession is more dangerous than a poor woman without chastity.

▲ Happiness and beauty are by-products of life.

Anecdote of Clay Figure Zhang of Tianjin and G沽 163

— Qinglin

Chinese art, thousands of years ago, discovered extraordinary skills unmatched in ancient and modern times. It is a pity that they all embraced secrecy, unwilling to make them public, especially to pass them on to those with different surnames. If the descendants are unworthy and there is no one to inherit, the art will be lost. Foreigners, on the other hand, have repeatedly inherited and adapted them, making significant inventions. This is truly regrettable. For example, in the western part of Tianjin, there was a craftsman named Zhang Mingshan who specialized in sculpting clay figures. However, his name was not widely known; people only knew his surname, so he was called Clay Figure Zhang. His skills are now lost. Although his descendants still engage in this craft, their work is unremarkable. I once recorded his sculpting methods and the figures he sculpted, detailing them in a certain newspaper. This can certainly promote the reputation of the Chinese art world. It is said that he had another anecdote, which I am now recording. It may well be a piece of historical material about a famous figure in the art world.

Li Hongzhang, the Governor-General of Zhili, heard of his reputation and summoned him to his office, intending to have him sculpt a clay figure of Zhang to sit opposite him. Zhang casually agreed, carefully examining Li's face for a short while, and then asked for a price of two thousand taels of gold. Li thought it was too expensive and refused. Zhang said nothing, bowed, and left. The next day, it was widely rumored that a clay statue of the Grand Secretary was displayed in Zhang's shop, its eyebrows and eyes animated, as if it were alive, with a price tag for sale. Onlookers crowded around. It turned out that Zhang had hidden clay in his sleeve when he visited Li. During the meeting, he had already sculpted Li's face and expression in his sleeve. Upon returning, he further contemplated his appearance, adding decorations and sculpting the body, arranging the clothes and headdress. Every detail was meticulously replicated. The artistry of his skill was such. Li was displeased upon hearing this, but there was nothing he could do. He quickly ordered someone to take two thousand taels of gold, go to the market, buy the statue, and place it on his desk. Every time he looked at the incarnation, he was amazed and admired it. There was a salt merchant from Changlu, a chief commissioner named Li, who also wanted Zhang to sculpt a statue of him. Zhang, known for his arrogance, said, "This Li is not that Li. Everyone knows that salt merchants are stingy. If I were to sculpt your esteemed likeness today, it would not be worth it unless you paid ten times the price of the Grand Secretary Li. Otherwise, there will be others who admire your countenance and buy it for their appreciation." Li was displeased with his disrespectful words, and angrily turned away, saying, "Tomorrow, Zhang will apply to this Li what he applied to that Li." But Li was petty and filed a lawsuit out of anger. Moreover, he was rich and arrogant, willing to sacrifice everything. He secretly bribed the officials with gold at night, and Zhang lost the lawsuit. He died in prison out of resentment.

Early Spring Recipes 164

— Yang Yixiao

▲ Soy Sauce Braised Pork: Take fresh pork, cut it into square chunks, and add pork bones. Add old broth and soy sauce, and braise over low heat for a long time. Once cooked, take it out. The taste is exceptionally rich and delicious.

▲ Fried Small Fish: The small fish are about an inch long, fleshy, and boneless. Commonly known as "meat-filled fish." Marinate them in sugar, vinegar, and good soy sauce in the morning. Fry them in oil in the afternoon until lightly browned. Sprinkle with a little licorice and fennel powder. They are fragrant and fresh.

▲ Fermented Snail: Snails have their tails snipped off, placed in a wok and stir-fried. Add fermented rice wine broth and a piece of raw lard. Cook until the flavor is very fresh and delicious.

▲ Fresh Broad Beans: Shell the broad beans, and stir-fry with bamboo shoot pieces. Add soy oil, soy sauce, and white sugar to the wok. Cook for two to three minutes. They are fresh, tender, and palatable.

▲ Silver Fish and Green Fish Stir-fry: Stir-fry silver fish and green fish with a little soy oil and soy sauce. It has a unique flavor.

▲ Clam Meat Stewed with Salted Fresh Meat: Dice both clam meat and salted fresh meat into small squares. Place them in a clay pot. Add a pinch of salt. Simmer over a charcoal stove until cooked. The taste is especially delicious.

Cheapest Items in He City 165

— Shuanghong

The cost of living is rising daily. Compared to decades ago, today's prices are incalculable. However, prices were cheap in the past, but there were even cheaper items among them. Even recalling them now brings lingering admiration.

▲ Suzhou Boat Cuisine with Four Powders and Four Noodles for Ten Copper Coins: Famous far and wide. Their pastries were especially delicious. Generally, each serving consisted of four types made from flour and four types made from dough. They were called "Four Powders and Four Noodles." Once, a friend jokingly said that he could buy "Four Powders and Four Noodles" for ten copper coins. When asked how, he replied: "One copper coin for a large glutinous rice ball filled with white sugar; one copper coin for two small rice dumplings from the wine dregs vendor; one copper coin for two fried rice cakes; two copper coins for a small steamer of 'dou gao' (bean flour cake). These are the 'Four Powders.' One copper coin for a small salted cake (a small round flatbread with scallion and lard, sprinkled with sesame seeds; the taste is very good); one copper coin for two fried chestnut sticks; one copper coin for a piece of 'guo kuai' (a coarse wheat cake, lightly sprinkled with salt, the only filling food for the poor; each whole cake sells for four copper coins, cut into four pieces for retail.)" (The above four items are all available at the flatbread stalls.) At the time, I greatly admired his cleverness. Now, only fried chestnut sticks are occasionally seen, but each one costs two copper coins. The rest have all been naturally eliminated.

▲ Two Items Did Not Increase in Price While Everything Else Did: In the early years of the Republic, someone said that everything had increased in price except for two items. When asked what they were, he replied: "The bamboo ear picks sold by beggars still sell for one copper coin, just as they always have. The almanacs hawked in tea houses at the end of the year still sell for three or four copper coins for the cheapest ones. Haven't these two items not increased in price?" Now, the old-style almanacs are gone, and even a bamboo ear pick costs two copper coins.

Other items, such as one egg, formerly sold for four or five copper coins; braised pork in soy sauce from Lu Gaojian, each piece selling for seven copper coins; and a large bowl of stir-fried fish and braised meat, selling for twenty-four copper coins, were all cheap and delicious. Now, all of these have increased tenfold or so. How can families of moderate means and below not lament the difficulty of making ends meet?

Scraps from the Military Medical Conference 166

— Huizi

The national army hospital directors' conference convened by the Ministry of War is a preliminary step towards the military medical conference. This conference will prepare various proposals to be solemnly resolved at the national military medical conference. Major issues such as the treatment of wounded and sick soldiers, the revision of military medical personnel, the replenishment of medical equipment, and the statistics of wounded and sick soldiers must be thoroughly planned and resolved.

The conference lasted four days and resolved no fewer than fifty important cases. However, the first step is to raise a sum of money. For example, building hospitals, purchasing X-ray machines, and improving food supplies all require money. However, the national treasury is currently tight, and all expenses are being reduced. Where can we find extra funds to improve and develop? This cannot be compared with the newly established Military Medical Supervisory Department, which has full access to funds. It is said that the department's planned model military hospital requires only 1.3 million yuan in start-up costs, compared with the 3,000 yuan start-up costs for each military hospital established by the Ministry of War. This is like a small sorcerer seeing a great wizard, an immeasurable difference.

The Central Hospital in the capital, formerly known as the Model Central Hospital, is the largest in scale among all public and private hospitals in Beijing. The head nurse's salary is over 200 yuan. As for the salaries of doctors in various departments, only the Minister and Vice Minister of the Ministry of War can compare. The Vice Minister is a lieutenant general and earns only 500 yuan per month, while the doctors in the hospital earn up to 600 yuan per month. However, their achievements over the past year have been mediocre. Last year, when wounded soldiers were crowded, the Ministry of War's hospitals accommodated up to 50,000 wounded soldiers, with a total monthly expenditure of only 300,000 yuan. The Central Hospital only accommodated 300 wounded soldiers, but its monthly expenditure was 150,000 yuan.

The attendees of this military medical conference were the directors of army hospitals from all over the country, a total of eighteen people. In terms of province of origin, Zhejiang was the most numerous. In terms of educational background, graduates of military medical schools accounted for one-third. However, one common point was that they were all German- or Japanese-trained medical scholars. Chief Secretary Jiang Qiuran first graduated from the Japanese Military Academy and then transferred to the Japanese Chiba Medical College, so he deserves to be a veteran expert in both military and medical affairs. The three heroes of the military medical community refer to Jiang, Hao Zihua, and Liu Jixiong. The conference secretaries, Wu Yubai and Yang Buping, are both well-known in the military medical community. The attendees of this conference are all leading figures in the military medical community, known as the "Eighteen Scholars, Four Talents, and Eight Sages." The "Eighteen Scholars" refer to the eighteen hospital directors who attended the conference. Wu and Yang are both figures among the "Four Talents and Eight Sages." Unfortunately, as an outsider, I did not inquire about the details from insiders and record them in detail.

Variations on Monkey's Opium Addiction 167

— Li Xufan

The harm of opium is known to everyone. All animals seem to be easily addicted, but what happens to their internal organs? Everyone seems to be able to describe the details. When Ma Lianjia was the Governor of Anhui, the opium ban was greatly relaxed. Residents in northern Anhui, such as Hao and Wo, almost could not live without opium. There was no family without opium. There were even female beggars who begged for opium dregs instead of food. At that time, I was in Zhengyang and saw a monkey sentenced to death for opium addiction. It was quite amusing, so I recorded the true story.

Zhengyangguan belongs to Shouxian County, a large town in northern Anhui. There was a man named Shi in the town, who was moderately wealthy and had a severe opium addiction. He kept a male monkey that was very clever. Whenever Shi lay down on an opium couch, the monkey would be with him. Occasionally, when Shi went to the opium den, the monkey would follow. One day, Shi went to the countryside for business and left the monkey at home. He did not return for one night. The next afternoon, the monkey could not bear it any longer and ran to the opium den. It placed a silver coin on the couch and cried wildly. The opium den owner knew it was Shi's monkey and was surprised. He tried to give it opium smoke. The monkey gladly accepted it. The owner gave it several puffs, and the monkey was overjoyed. It secretly returned home, and the family did not know. This went on for three days. The opium addicts regarded the monkey as a comrade. On the third day, while the monkey was receiving the opium smoke, the owner suddenly arrived. The monkey was shocked to see him and turned away and fled. The opium den owner told Shi the truth. Shi was furious. He checked his pillow and found three silver coins missing, knowing that the monkey had stolen them. The monkey was afraid of causing trouble and hid all day. Shi thought that the monkey had become addicted to opium and was now acting like a thief on the roof. Its cleverness was endearing, but its behavior was unacceptable. Afraid that it would cause unexpected trouble in the future, Shi took a sharp knife the next day and stabbed the monkey to death unexpectedly. He then took the monkey's internal organs and hung them on a tree to observe any changes. After a while, he gradually saw the surface of the lungs wriggling, as if ants were gathering. It was difficult to discern what was happening. Shi blew several puffs of opium smoke on it, and the wriggling gradually stopped. The neighbors gathered to watch, and it became a popular story. My residence was very close to Shi's house. After witnessing this, I intended to take the monkey's organs back to study them, but because the town was a remote mountain village, there was no scientific hospital, so I abandoned the idea. Monkeys are intelligent animals, and their blood vessels and bones are not very different from those of humans. They can be addicted to the same habits as humans. When opium poisons humans, does it cause the same changes? I cannot help but worry about this.

Warmth in the Heart (385) 168

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Seventeen: The Art of Preserving Youth: Emeralds and Black Ink Mix in Her Brows; The Way to Extend Life is Unavailable: Golden Market with Fine Horses

The first person to know was Gai Yutang. He and Pan's grandmother's husband were in the same business. As the saying goes, "One who is near the water gets the moon first." He ran to Pan's house and cried loudly, showing his straightforward nature of a Northerner. Pan's grandmother said, "Now that the person is dead, can crying bring him back to life? However, you should understand why Old Six couldn't stay in Shanghai and had to travel all the way to Beijing. You should understand that." Gai Yutang said, "This is our fault, but Old Six is like a wild horse, and no one can tie him down. You know that." Later, the carriage owner, A Sen, also learned the news. Pan's grandmother also blamed him in the same way. She said, "Although a person's life is destined, if Old Six had died in Shanghai, he would have had many relatives by his side. It wouldn't be like dying alone in a foreign land." A Sen also bowed his head in silence. When Hua Lao Liu's coffin was transported from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Shanghai, both of them received the news. Gai Yutang said, "When he was alive, I was sorry for him. After death, it should be my responsibility." A Sen said, "No. Old Six's coffin should be my responsibility. I have a piece of land in Jiangwan. I can bury him there." Gai Yutang said, "I will not return to the North in the future. I can buy a piece of land and bury him properly. Now his coffin is temporarily placed in the guild hall. I will pay for the coffin's storage." A Sen said, "I knew him first. Naturally, it is up to me to take care of his coffin." The two argued endlessly. Pan's grandmother said, "What are you arguing about now as if it were a big deal? You both wanted to take advantage of him in the first place. When he went to Beijing, you didn't come out to help him. Moreover, if it weren't for the two of you, why would he have had to go to Beijing? Now that someone has bought a coffin for him and transported it to the South, you want to be good people. People will say that you have a conscience towards Hua Lao Liu. Touch your own conscience. Now I will take charge for the deceased. I don't want either of you to interfere. We are from Changshu. She and I were good sisters. I will transport her coffin back to Changshu. I have a piece of vacant land there. I will bury her there. You don't need to worry about it. You are happy for a moment, but I am afraid that you will leave it in the guild hall and not even visit her grave. In Changshu, when I go to sweep the grave, I will burn some paper money in front of her grave." Later, Pan's grandmother indeed transported Hua Yuanchun's coffin back to Changshu for burial. This concluded the matter of Hua Yuanchun. Green Ripple could not know these details. Later, someone told Zuo Shichen, who then passed it on. The women in the brothels were originally good daughters, but the evil society led them to the abyss of depravity. It is unknown how many have lost their youth. It is precisely:

Mountain flowers eat away at the bones of beautiful women,

A wild burial bewilders the souls of wandering sons.

How will the matter unfold? Listen to the next chapter for the resolution.

Financial and Gold Market Ending Weak 169

Falling Twelve Taels Weak

Yesterday, March 18th, the gold price rose and fell. The market situation was uncertain, with fluctuations of ten taels. The total market difference was twenty-four or five taels, eventually falling twelve taels. The foreign exchange turned good, and the listed prices shrank by one level, reflecting a situation of tight external conditions but relaxed internal conditions. There were significant differences in market trading compared to the previous market. Companies like Yuanmao and Shuiyuan Sheng bought in, while Zhifeng, Yongchang, Yu Yongheng, and others sold. Although the overseas silver market fell, it was not affected. The gold price was initially stable, but the buying surged, and the exchange rate was also good, causing a sudden increase of ten taels to six hundred ninety-seven or eight taels. The subsequent fluctuations were severe, hovering around ninety taels. Later, as the exchange rate declined, it plunged sharply, breaking through eighty taels. Since the market will be closed on Wednesday, the situation is relatively stable, with only four or five taels of fluctuations. The final calculation seems to be six hundred seventy-five taels. It is said that today's major trends may not be too volatile.

Once Struggling in the Morning

The opening price for May this morning was six hundred eighty-seven taels and five mace, the same as the closing price last night. The main price only fell by one-quarter of a mace. The silver price fell by one cent, and the private telegrams fell by eight-sevenths of a cent. The people's confidence was stable. There were three or four taels of fluctuation from ninety-two taels to eighty-eight taels. There were buyers, especially for British gold. First, Sanlin bought June's at 14125, then the British and Japanese banks traded at 140625. Zhejiang once bought at 13.9375. The people's confidence was boosted, and the price soared by eight or nine taels to ninety-seven taels and eight mace at twenty minutes past nine. Shortly after, Shunli and Wanyu and others came to sell. In a short time, it fell by six taels. When the first order was announced, the listed price was ninety-two taels. Although the hanging price was reduced by two-five U.S. dollars and five jiao, the Japanese gold added two fen and two-five, the public was not convinced, and the price was suppressed by one tael. But it was immediately increased to ninety-three taels and five mace for retail buyers. Fuchang and others came to sell in an instant. From forty minutes to fifty minutes past nine, the price plummeted by more than nine taels to eighty-four taels because the exchange rate was not easy to sell. Then, Yuanheng, Hengyu, and others bought in, and the banks traded five or six months of British gold at 140625, and it was ninety-three taels and five mace again at ten o'clock. Suddenly, there was another sign of weakness, which was sold by Tong Taichang, Hengxing, Yuan, and other items. So at half past ten, it fell back to eighty-five taels and immediately jumped up five or six taels. Wanxing, Shunli, Yuancheng, and Yonglai bought in at forty minutes past ten to ninety taels. Afterwards, the fatigue was fully revealed. The British gold was even sold off. The Chinese and Japanese banks traded six months of U.S. dollars at thirty-two yuan and seventy-five. Sumitomo bought May's British gold at 1425, then 25 could be settled, and the selling wind in the field became more intense. Zhifeng, Yongqian, Changxiang, Fuxing, Yongyu, and others all sold. From the third quarter to the third quarter past eleven, the price fell by sixteen taels in one hour, only seventy-five taels, and then added to seven and a half taels. At noon, the market closed at seventy-six taels, and the announced price was changed to seven hundred forty-five taels and eight mace. It is estimated that it was suppressed by fifty-five taels to fifty-two or three taels at noon and seventy taels.

Depressed After Market

The market opened at seventy-five taels and five mace in the afternoon. Later, because the Indian exchange rate was seen to fall by three or four Anna, it rose to seventy-eight taels and eight or nine mace, and immediately fell back to seventy-three taels and two or three mace. Because the Indian exchange rate was reported to have risen by six Anna, Yuanmao Yong and others came in and added to seven and a half taels. At the third quarter past two, it returned to five and a half taels. In fact, the people's minds were distracted and swayed with the wind. After three o'clock, it was suddenly heard that the Indian exchange rate had plummeted. In an instant, it rose by five taels to eighty-one taels and eight mace, because Dalian Gang suddenly let go and bought. After learning that the rumor had been refuted and had been depreciated by three taels, it was estimated at seventy-nine taels. Later, Xinhang bought in and added to eighty taels. In an instant, it dropped by more than three taels. It is estimated that the Indian exchange rate was indeed three Anna, estimated at seventy-six taels and five o'clock. There was a slight head start, and it was seventy-nine taels at half past four o'clock, and the market closed at the softening state, estimated at seventy-five taels and eight mace. Circulation Letter and Consultation 184

-- Yang Yanhe

▲ To Mr. Liu Runsheng Jiu, the treatment method for nasal congestion is as follows: 1. Every morning, use finely ground edible salt to brush your teeth, spit it into your hand, and wash your face, paying close attention to rubbing the nasal area for a long time. This is effective. 2. Grind one tael of gardenia seeds into a fine powder, melt yellow wax into pills the size of parasol seeds, and take ten or twenty pills with clear tea after dinner. 3. Grind two qian of realgar, eight fen of alum, two qian of sulfur, eight fen of frankincense, two qian of almonds, one qian of rhubarb, seven qian of borax, four fen of light powder, and one qian of copper wire into a fine powder, mix with honey and wine, apply it to the affected area before going to bed, and wash it off the next morning. Do not interrupt the treatment.

▲ To Mr. Zhu Jingnian, for hemorrhoids without pain or itching, only bleeding, Chuan Gui pills are the main treatment. In addition, sprinkling with dried hemorrhoid powder should promote recovery.

▲ To Mr. Li Yiyi, abdominal pain that lessens after eating and is relieved by hand pressure indicates cold. Pain that worsens after eating and is also worsened by pressing indicates food accumulation. Dizziness with a stringy and slippery pulse indicates phlegm accumulation. A hot feeling in the abdomen that makes it impossible to touch indicates accumulated heat. Heavy lifting, strenuous effort, or accidental injuries indicate blood stasis. A lump in the abdomen that disappears upon pressing, with spider veins on the surface, indicates worm infestation. Treatment should be tailored to the specific condition and cannot be generalized.

▲ To Mr. Wu Xinfa, this condition requires emphasis on recuperation and cannot solely rely on medication. You can take 50 cypress heart-nourishing pills with longan soup on alternate evenings, and 3 qian of Jinggong Miaoxiang powder mixed with boiled water on the other evenings. As for the marriage issue, it should be done when the time is right. If circumstances limit it, delaying it slightly is also acceptable, but maintaining a clear mind and enduring hardship will naturally reduce desires.

▲ Note: Those asking about illness can directly write to Yang Yanhe, a medical doctor at No. 80 Anshun Lane, Kangti Road, and attach postage for a special reply. This publication will not collect the mail on behalf of you.

Youth Land

That Landlord 185

— Mr. Xiao

Several friends who used to gather together have now scattered due to various circumstances.

Reuniting with Mr. Hua and Mr. Xi in Shanghai brought an extraordinary joy to Xiao's heart, like a spring tide overflowing.

Xiao was a young man who had just come from the interior. His travel expenses were limited, and he was unfamiliar with the people and the place, all of which made him frown. Moreover, Shanghai was a dividing line between heaven and hell. Without money, one was fully qualified to be among the starving. This terror gradually eroded Xiao's heart. Besides finding friends, there was no other way for this person to go. So, after staying in the inn for a day, Xiao planned for the whole day, waiting until the afternoon to see that the rain had stopped before going out. The sky was gloomy, and the road was wet. To avoid any inconvenience, he immediately got into a rickshaw.

Soon, the journey shortened with time. Young Xiao met Mr. Hua on the second floor where he lived. The upstairs was full of books, dominated entirely by humor. Although five or three people were sitting separately at their respective tables, the only sound was the scratching of Hua's pen on paper. Xiao took off his hat and came in. Because he was wearing rubber-soled shoes, the rustling of his footsteps was also muffled. At this moment, Hua's wife suddenly turned her head from the mirror and saw Xiao.

After they exchanged greetings in a dialect, Hua raised his deeply nearsighted eyes from the desk and suddenly stood up.

The room was naturally filled with laughter. Xiao, who could not bear loneliness, burst out laughing loudly. It seemed that all the words he wanted to say were expressed in laughter. Everyone looked at each other's faces, and everyone felt the joy of reunion.

"Absence is a mirror," Hua said. Xiao's emaciated appearance aroused some sadness in the young Xiao's heart. But their questions to Xiao did not stop because Xiao was touching and pressing his cheeks with his hands. They continued to ask:

"Xiao, it's good that you could come resolutely this time."

"If I hadn't come, there would have been no way to think about it at home."

"Then your family is still managed by your mother?"

Yes, this young Xiao gave his mother only a home and not a penny. Even his own travel expenses were all included in the family expenses. From then on, the family's situation was unimaginable. There were many, many shortcomings and many hardships placed on her. Could this sorrow find a resting place in Xiao's heart? It was always like a burst of storms, forever unable to wash away the mud on the road. Well, young Xiao was already approaching middle age. From another perspective, he was using his parents' money to do things without knowing the hardships of the world. Understanding was like being a fool. Only then could one be considered young. Xiao's thoughtfulness was a special gift from heaven. Others did not need such cleverness. Others were rich and could use money to buy obedience and cover up their faults. But for Xiao, it was very different. He used to fret over petty things as a small clerk for a few tens of dollars, watching people's faces. He did not lack the good character that a clerk should have. It would not do to ask such a person to wave flags and shout for revolution. People looking at him seemed to think he was solemn and rigorous, like a clerk talking to his superior. At first glance, people suspected that he was deliberately being restrained. Sometimes, his wild laughter was an exception. After a long time of not seeing Xiao, his friend Mr. Hua saw that he seemed to have become two different people. This young man, who was not what he seemed, had changed too quickly and too suddenly. So, seeing him again actually increased a faint sadness. In Hua's keen eyes, he could see some of the unspoken sadness. They borrowed cigarettes, looking at the smoke they exhaled spinning around. Xiao also looked at Hua's father, as if he had gained something.

This was an old man who still did not forget to shave despite his age. They often met in the provincial capital. Here, his face was fuller, and he looked better than before. This was what Xiao saw, so he asked him how many bowls of rice he ate every day. Being so plump and fair was related to his appetite. When the young Xiao sat down at the dinner table, seeing all the meat and fish was of no use. He secretly sighed at his own appetite. This kind of person seemed to want to become an immortal. Immortals do not eat worldly food. This dinner was equivalent to his midnight snack.

After finishing dinner, he tiptoed to the window and stood there blankly, as if recalling something. Seeing that it was completely dark outside, he remembered the time. Therefore, he shouted that he wanted to go back to the inn. Hua's wife brought an orange behind him and told him to sit down, insisting that he stay for a while. Hua still had a manuscript to finish and wanted to show it to him. Only then did he win back the heart of this person who insisted on leaving. He casually flipped through a book on the bookshelf. The words on the book were still blurry, like reading a newspaper, picking and choosing articles to read. In the midst of speaking, he read the entire thing to Hua for his creation.

Hua's wife was an extremely good person. She had been busy all day preparing the dishes for Xiao to eat. She also grabbed handfuls of melon seeds from the drawer and piled them on the table for Xiao to eat. Xiao, because he had something on his mind, did not smoke. He cracked the melon seeds one by one from his mouth and threw the kernels on the ground. He remained silent, close to a silent demeanor. In the silence, there were things that were not silent. At this time, the landlord downstairs seemed to be arguing over a small matter, deliberately making noise for the writers upstairs to hear. They loudly scolded, calling out to both men and women, unwilling to let go. It seemed very sad. If the writer could capture them in a novel at another time, their story would be hilariously funny. Because he was in the middle of writing a story and was stuck on the central part, he frowned and thought, regardless. It was not easy to complete his own 5,000-word creation. He lengthened his face, feeling that there were many trivial matters between husband and wife and that they were difficult to handle. For example, the man had a bad temper. When he encountered something slightly unsatisfactory, he would smash bowls and throw pots. Could the woman use gentleness to ease the situation? Hua's wife was quite aware of this kind of thing. Before he could speak, she laughed out loud. This laughter was laughing at that landlord with a crowd of children. He had drunk too much wine and walked in staggering from outside. The woman who opened the door was patted on the shoulder by the man, as if he wanted to make up for all the unrestrained and outrageous behavior outside on her. With a mouthful of wine, the round face covered in fragrant powder would naturally dodge away, using all kinds of shields to resist. The man became annoyed. The man seemed like a lion, jumping and roaring for a while. The other party's policy seemed to unintentionally subdue the furious person. In a matter of tens of minutes, such a big and unclear change could occur. For those whose policy had already taken effect, even if the man had thrown a tantrum, saying this was not okay and that was not okay, the woman only needed to grab her man's weakness and show him a little bit of affection, catering to his preferences. For a husband who saw his wife doing this, he would not want to stop and would stop. A heart of love would naturally follow the act of apologizing, taking root and sprouting. In the end, the couple was still whispering and talking about things that others could not hear.

Originally, when a couple quarreled and sulked, once they slept in bed, they would reconcile without the need for outsiders to mediate. There were many such things.

Therefore, the writer upstairs seemed to put down his pen, waiting for the rain to pass before starting to work again. He was very similar in demeanor. He did not speak or laugh. The downstairs was so quiet that he could hear the mice squeaking and fighting. The story that the writer was writing continued to be completed. He read it to Xiao while tapping his foot on the floor, making a rhythmic sound. A day and a night's work was compensated by the fee for these 5,000 words. Xiao and everyone exhaled a sigh of relief, indicating that this matter was resolved and that everyone should return to their beds and have some husbandly dreams. But suddenly, he remembered that he could not find his wife here. A thin bedding was still left in the inn. There was no need to say that he wanted to go back. The writer also understood. The writer looked at the stacks of manuscript paper he had written and then looked at the bed with the low-hanging curtains. His wife was sleeping there alone, waiting. It would not be too presumptuous to say "waiting," would it? Being inseparable was what a good couple should be like. It seemed that it should be so. The two of them were especially close and intimate. Because he was afraid of delaying his friend's affairs, Xiao quietly left.

Toothache 186

— Siyong

I, who had never suffered from toothache, was once confronted by facts that did not prevent this small disease from causing people so much pain.

A few days ago, this tooth was already aching faintly, but I did not feel any inconvenience when eating. Who knew that the pain would gradually increase around ten o'clock last night. Later, it became tighter and tighter, and I could no longer continue writing. I put down my pen and went to bed, but how could I fall asleep? Turning this way, turning that way, lying on my back, lying on my stomach - I tried all possible sleeping positions, but I still could not fall asleep. The more I could not fall asleep, the more severe the pain became. The more severe the pain became, the more I could not fall asleep. While tossing and turning, the roosters crowed in the distance. I got up from the bed, and the window screen revealed the light of dawn. The cold air of the severe winter threatened me, and I slipped back into bed, opening my eyes to watch the sky slowly brighten.

Later, I was truly exhausted and fell into a hazy sleep. But soon I was awakened by the pain. After waking up from the pain, I changed my body position. Later, I fell asleep again, but I was awakened by the pain again. This entire body, eager for rest, seemed to be dominated by a small aching tooth. One foot entered the dream, and the other followed. It dragged and pulled it out of the dream. One escaped, and the other chased. I don't know how many times this happened.

The clock struck ten, and the pain had not diminished slightly. The clock struck eleven, and it was still the same. When the mouth covered the left cheek, I could hear the thumping sound of the pain. I was too lazy to get up and lay there like death.

"Siyong, are you awake? Let me see."

Mother sat on the edge of my bed and leaned her head in to look at my face.

Afterward, Mother prepared a bowl of salt water, saying that it was the most effective medicine for toothache. She took a spoonful and poured it into my mouth, teaching me to tilt my head back so that the salt water would completely pour into the painful area. I held it until it was very hot and then spat it out. I replaced it and held it like this four times.

However, holding it did not reduce the pain at all. After holding it four times, it was still ineffective.

"Get up and eat. I'll have your sister cook porridge for you."

Lying down hurt, and getting up hurt. Hearing my mother's words, I reluctantly got up.

The porridge was very hot. I stirred it in the bowl with chopsticks, blowing air with my mouth. The more I blew air with my mouth, the more the tooth ached. And the air I blew out was no longer as strong and forceful as usual. It was very weak, almost unable to stir the thin porridge slightly. In front of me was a steaming bowl of thin porridge and several plates of dishes. I frowned, only looking at them. I remembered a story that my father's friend, Doctor Hu, told me when I was young. He said that there was a teacher whose employer was very stingy. The dishes were not good, and there was no rice every day. He was only served porridge. The porridge was so thin that he would be hungry after a while. Once, the teacher tapped his chopsticks on the bowl and recited a poem to the porridge:

"A grain of rice is cooked into a large bowl,

The breeze from the nose brings undulating waves.

It looks like a bronze mirror,

With whiskers and eyebrows fully reflected inside."

Although the verse was not well-crafted, the teacher's description of the thin porridge was truly vivid.

The porridge had cooled to lukewarm. It was thin and soft and could be swallowed relatively smoothly. But eating the dishes was annoying. When I picked up a piece of vegetable and put it in my mouth, even if I chewed it slightly with the teeth on the right side, it would affect the painful tooth on the left side, and the pain would increase sharply. So, I swallowed the vegetables whole.

The pain was still the same, and it gradually felt somewhat worse. Could I continue to bear this pain? So, I took down a large pile of dust-covered tested remedies and household knowledge from the corner of the bookshelf and flipped through them. These books contained many prescriptions for toothache. The medicines in the prescriptions were either impossible to find temporarily or the preparation procedures were extremely complicated. Each prescription claimed to be a hundred percent effective and miraculously effective. I was afraid of being fooled, so I flipped through one book after another and rejected them all. Finally, in the seventh collection of household knowledge, I discovered a "street laugh" that someone had circled with a pen, saying… If you rub it with top-quality borneol and a little cinnabar, it will have a miraculous effect and cure both wind-fire and worm teeth… It is truly worthy of being called a "street laugh" that heals over time… The long two lines of close circles seemed to hide some magic, and I couldn't help but feel some faith in this "street laugh." I immediately bought top-quality borneol and cinnabar, rubbed them with my finger, and rubbed them on once, twice… seven times, eight times… even dozens of times, until my mouth was filled with the intense and unbearable smell of borneol, and the saliva and cinnabar formed something like blood. And the painful tooth became even more painful, even more painful. I believed that this "street laugh" could cure it, but the more I rubbed, the more painful it became. I couldn't sit, and I couldn't stand. I walked from this room to that room, as pitiful as an injured sheep.

At dinner, Grandmother and Mother persuaded me to eat some rice. They said that rice was more nutritious than porridge. But how could I eat it? Grandmother said,

"I don't have a single tooth left. Whether I eat vegetables or rice, I swallow them all."

Grandmother is seventy years old this year, but I didn't know that she ate like this. Can the taste of rice, the taste of vegetables, and the taste of all foods be properly appreciated without careful chewing? From this, it can be seen that all the joys of life for the elderly are as dim as the fading evening glow in the sky after sunset. And we young people are fortunate. Although I am now in the same position as my grandmother when eating, even worse than my grandmother.

After dinner, Mr. Xiancheng came to visit. He heard that I had a toothache and specially went home to get some medicine water and a few aspirins for me. I am grateful to my many friends. They all treat me so kindly.

I rubbed the medicine water several times and took two aspirins. It really felt much better. When the clock struck nine, I went to bed. Extreme fatigue led me to fall asleep immediately. But after sleeping for a while, I woke up from the pain again. It turned out that all so-called toothache medicines were nothing more than anesthetics. The salt water that Mother valued, the borneol and cinnabar of the "street laugh," and the medicine water containing the aroma of chloroform that Mr. Xiancheng brought - their effectiveness was determined by the strength of their anesthetic power. My toothache was so severe that the salt water and borneol were of no use.
